in initiating the greeting of peace and replying it back with non-Muslims

  ABSTRACT:

This is a critical study of the แธฅadฤซth narrated by Suhayl b. Abฤซ แนขฤliแธฅ, from his dad, from Abลซ Hurayrah: โdo not initiate the greeting of peace* (al-Salฤm) with polytheistsโ, which Muslim included in his แนขaแธฅฤซแธฅ, and which had some differences in wording between its different narrators. It was also used in argumentation by those who maintained that it was categorically forbidden to initiate the greeting of peace with non-Muslims, even do there exists a number of other authentic แธฅadฤซths that command spreading the greeting of peace. It may seem that there exists an apparent contradiction between them, which is the reason that led the present author to study this แธฅadฤซth, and elucidate the differences that appeared in its different narrations, and resolving its conflict with the other แธฅadฤซths on extending and spreading the greeting of peace and returning it back with non-Muslims, as mentioned in the Prophetic Sunnah. All of this with the objective that the present study fulfills all the needs in determining every authentic แธฅadฤซths on this topic.

  INTRODUCTION:

All praise be to God, the Lord of all creation, and may peace and blessings be upon the Trustworthy Messenger, his family, his companions and all those who follow him:

This is a critical study of the แธฅadฤซth narrated by Suhayl b. Abฤซ แนขฤliแธฅ, from his dad, from Abลซ Hurayrah: โdo not initiate the greeting of peace with polytheists โ and in another narration: Christians and Jews. And when you meet any of them in the road, then make him take its narrowest path.โ

The need for knowing the ruling on such a matter, that causes much is very clear considering that people mixed with each other to a degree unseen throughout history. [review] And Muslims spread across all countries, dealing and working with others from other religions, and maybe they were discomforted due to especially if the context required that, such as if they . contradicts the generality of the Qurสพฤnic and Prophetic texts that command spreading the greeting of peace between people. Ibn แธคajar mentioned the differing of the Pious Predecessors (Salaf) on this issue due to the conflict between the apparent meaning of the texts, he said, โForbidding the initiation of the greeting of peace with non-Muslims was explicitly mentioned in what was included by Muslim and al-Bukhฤrฤซ in his al-Adab al-Mufrad, from a path via Suhayl b. Abฤซ แนขฤliแธฅ , from his dad, from Abลซ Hurayrah, โdo not initiate the greeting of peace with Christians and Jews. And when you meet any of them in the road, then make him take its narrowest path.โ ... And a group of scholars maintained that it was permissible to initiate the greeting of peace (al-Salฤm) with them: al-แนฌabarฤซ related from Ibn สฟUyaynah: โItโs permissible to initiate the greeting of peace with unbelievers based on the verse, โGod does not forbid you to deal kindly and justly with anyone who has not fought you...โ, and Abrahamโs statement to his [non-Muslim] dad, โPeace be with youโ.โ And al-Bayhaqฤซ said after mentioning the แธฅadฤซth of Abลซ สพUmฤmah that he used to initiate the greeting of peace with everyone that he passed by, and when he was asked about that he replied, โGod made peace the greeting of our community (ummah), and a safety for the [non-Muslim] people under our protection.โ That was the opinion of the Abลซ สพUmฤmah, and the แธฅadฤซth of Abลซ Hurayrah on prohibiting its initiation is . And [al-Qฤdฤซ] สฟIyฤแธ responded concerning the verse and the saying of Abraham โ upon him be peace โ to his dad that the intention from that was distancing , the intention was not to greet. And some of the Salaf stated that the verse, โand say, โPeaceโ: they will come to know.โ was abrogated by the verse on qitฤl.โ[1]

The clash between the evidence pointing out to the prohibition of initiating the greeting of peace with them, on the one hand, and the permissibility of initiating it on the other, reached the point where those who argued for the prohibition claimed the occurence of abrogation, and the claim by others that there was a restriction, and another group went to provide different interpretations of the verses.   I. GATHERING THE NARRATIONS OF SUHAYLโS แธคADฤชTH:

This แธฅadฤซth doesn't appear with that wording except from the narration of Suhayl b. Abฤซ แนขฤliแธฅ, from his dad, from Abลซ Hurayrah

  II. TEXTS THAT CONTRADICT SUHAILโS แธคADฤชTH:

The apparent meaning of the แธฅadฤซth of Suhayl is contradicted by a number of other more general and more explicit แธฅadฤซths that command spreading the greeting of peace, and which have more authentic chains of transmission (isnฤds), among which:

  1. The แธฅadฤซth of al-Barฤสพ in the แนขaแธฅฤซแธฅayn: โThe Messenger of God ๏ทบ commanded us to do seven things: ... and spreading the greeting of peace.โ[59]
  2. The แธฅadฤซth of สฟAbd Allฤh b. Salฤm, that the first thing that the Messenger of God ๏ทบ said in his first day in the city of al-Madฤซnah: โO People! Spread greetings of peace, feed the hungry, uphold the ties of kinship, be in prayer when others are asleep, and youโll enter Paradise in peace.โ[60]
  3. The แธฅadฤซth of สฟAbd Allฤh b. สฟAmr, that a man asked the Messenger of God ๏ทบ โWhich quality of Islฤm is the best?โ, he responded, โTo feed the hungry and to greet with peace those you know and those you do not know.โ[61]

And these famous and authentic แธฅadฤซths all convey the generality of the command, and theyโre in perfect accordance with the apparent meaning of the Qurสพฤn, such as in this verse commanding with regards to polytheists to state: โPeace be with you! We do not seek the company of ignorant people,โ[62] and the verse: โbut turn away from them and say, โPeaceโ.โ[63]. Ibn Jarฤซr al-แนฌabarฤซ said interpreting the former, โโPeace be with you!โ where salฤm (peace) has the nominative reading (= salฤmun) by the pronoun โon youโ or โfor youโ.โ[64]

The แธฅadฤซth of Suhayl contains a restriction to the generality of these texts, whose apparent meaning encompasses both generality and total inclusion. it abrogates the ruling of these Qurสพฤnic verses, that allow initiating the greeting of peace with polytheists when turning away from them. and prohibited from initiating the greeting of peace with polytheists and People of the Book, and they donโt have any other evidence besides it.

A number of people from the Pious Predecessors (Salaf) argued about the permissibility of initiating the greeting of peace with polytheists based on the generality of these verses, examples include:

  1. From Shuสฟayb b. al-แธคabแธฅฤb, he said: I was with สฟAlฤซ b. สฟAbd Allฤh al-Bฤriqฤซy when a Jew or Christian passed by, and [สฟAlฤซ] greeted him. Shuสฟayb remarked: โโโโโHeโs a Jew or Christian!โ [สฟAlฤซ] responded by reciting to me the last of Sลซrat al-Zukhruf, โThe Prophet has said, โMy Lord, truly these are people who do not believe,โ but turn away from them and say, โPeaceโ: they will come to know.โ[65].[66]
  2. From al-Masสฟลซdฤซ, from สฟAwn b. สฟAbd Allฤh, he said: Muแธฅammad b. Kaสฟb asked สฟUmar b. สฟAbd al-สฟAzฤซz about initiating the greeting of peace with people of the covenant, he responded: โYou greet back, but you donโt initiate it.โ I said: What is you personal opinion? He replied: โI donโt see any issue with initiating it with them!โ I asked: Why? He responded by citing the verse, โbut turn away from them and say, โPeaceโ: they will come to know.โ[67]
  3. Ibn สฟUyaynah maintained that itโs permissible to initiate the greeting of peace with unbelievers based on the verse, โGod does not forbid you to deal kindly and justly with anyone who has not fought you...โ, and Abrahamโs statement to his dad, โPeace be with youโ.[68]

Some of the general แธฅadฤซths in spreading the greeting of peace contain many other commands, such as the แธฅadฤซth โWe were commanded to do seven things: ...โ The exegetes and jurists argued โO People! Spread greetings of peace, feed the hungry, uphold the ties of kinship.โ And itโs known that upholding the ties of kinship is obligatory โ even with non-Muslims, such as if oneโs parents were non-Muslim. The same can be said with regards to feeding the hungry, no one held that it was restricted only to Muslims, rather it is genereal even with non-Muslim, and itโs considered among the actions of kindness without any disagrement.

All these authentic แธฅadฤซths from these companions came in the context of after their treason in the battle of al-Khunduq, so he ordered the companions to not initiate the greeting of peace with them, and to make them the narrowest path of the road, since they're . non-Muslims under our protection, nor those with whom there's a treaty, nor the peaceful polytheists.

Isแธฅฤq b. Rฤhawayh explained

This was the same interpretation given by Shaykh al-Islฤm Ibn Taymiyyah as related by Ibn Qayyim โ I heard our Shaykh say that.โ[107]

ููุฐุง ูุณุฑ ุดูุฎ ุงูุฅุณูุงู ุงุจู ุชูููุฉ ุณุจุจ ูุฑูุฏ ุญุฏูุซ ุงูููู ุนู ุจุฏุก ุงููููุฏ ุจุงูุณูุงู ููุง ูููู ุนูู ุงุจู ุงูููู (ุฃูุง ููู ุงููุจู ูุง ุชุจุฏุคููู ุจุงูุณูุงูุ ููุฐุง ููุง ุฐูุจ ุฅูููู ููุญุงุฑุจูู ููู ูููุฏ ูุฑูุธุฉ ูุฃูุฑ ุฃูุง ูุจุฏุคูุง ุจุงูุณูุงูุ ูุฃูู ุฃูุงู ููู ูุฏ ุฐูุจ ูุญุฑุจููุ ุณูุนุช ุดูุฎูุง ูููู ุฐูู).[107]

Ibn Qayyim said: โIt was said that this was in a specific situation in which they marched to Banลซ Qurayแบah stating โdo not initiate the greeting of peace with themโ, as such, is it a general command for all people of the convenant? Or is it rather specific to a similar situation? This is a spot for consideration, Muslim narrated in his แนขaแธฅฤซแธฅ from the แธฅadฤซth of Abลซ Hurayrah that the Prophet ๏ทบ said, โdo not initiate the greeting of peace with with Christians or Jews. And when you meet any of them in the road, then make him take its narrowest path.โ What is apparent is that it's a general ruling. Both the pious predecessors and the successors differed on this matter, many of them held that we don't initiate the greeting of peace with them. Others however held that it was permissible to initiate it, just like for greeting them back with peace: This opinion was ascribed to Ibn สฟAbbฤs, Abลซ สพUmฤmah, Ibn Muแธฅayrฤซz, and it's a position in the school of al-Shฤfiสฟฤซ โ may God have mercy on him โ but the one who holds this view specified that only โpeace be upon youโ is said to him, without mentioning the mercy part and in the singular form. A group of other scholars said that itโs permissible to initiate the greeting of peace with non-Muslims if it serves a beneficial purpose or need, or if he fears he will be harmed by them, or if he has family relations with them, or for another reason for which itโs required. This was narrated by Ibrฤhฤซm al-Nakhaสฟฤซ and สฟAlqamah. al-สพAwzฤสฟฤซ declared: โIf you initiate the greeting of peace, then so did the righteous; and if you donโt initiate it, then so did the righteous.โ They also differed concerning the obligation of returning the greeting, with the majority maintaining that itโs obligatory โ and this is the correct view. And a group said: It is not obligatory to return the greeting with them, just as it isnโt obligatory with the people of heresy (ahl al-bidสฟah). But the correct view is the first one: the difference is that weโre commanded to forsake the people of heresy so as to deter and warn them [from their heresy], in contrast to the people of the covenant.โ[108]

What Isแธฅฤq b. Rฤhawayh, Shaykh al-Islฤm Ibn Taymiyyah and Ibn Qayyim mentioned regarding the context of this แธฅadฤซth is the correct view as proven by the other authentic narrations.

al-Bukhฤrฤซ included in a chapter titled โInitiating the greeting of peace in a gathering with both Muslims and polytheistsโ the แธฅadฤซth of สพUsฤmah b. Zayd where he narrates that the Prophet ๏ทบ was going to pay a visit to Saสฟd b. สฟUbฤdah (who was sick) after the battle of Badr, and that he โpassed by a gathering in which there were Muslims, pagan idolators and Jews, and among them there was สฟAbd Allฤh b. สพUbay b. Salลซl, and there was สฟAbd Allฤh b. Rawฤแธฅah too. When a cloud of dust raised by the animal covered that gathering, สฟAbd Allฤh b. สพUbay covered his nose with his sheet and said, โDonโt cover us with dust.โ The Prophet ๏ทบ greeted them with peace and then stopped, dismounted and invited them to God and also recited to them verses from the Qurสพฤn. สฟAbd Allฤh b. สพUbay b. Salลซl said, โO man! There is nothing better than what you say, if itโs the truth. So do not trouble us in our gatherings. Go back to your mount (or house,) and if anyone of us comes to you, then preach to him.โโ[109]

And al-Bayhaqฤซ narrated it with the wording: โThe Prophet ๏ทบ passed by a gathering with Muslims, Jews and polytheists, and he greeted all of them with peaceโ. al-Bayhaqฤซ notes that this was included in the two แนขaแธฅฤซแธฅs.[110] It's also included in the Muแนฃannaf of สฟAbd al-Razzฤq, but without the wording โall of themโ.[111]

And this is a practical Sunnah that confirms the generality of the Qurสพฤnic verses and the permissibility of initiating the greeting of peace with non-Muslims. Stating that the Prophet's ๏ทบ greeting of peace was only addressed towards those Muslims that were present [in the gathering] requires consideration, for it's not supported by the apparent meaning of the แธฅadฤซth: what is evident is that the gathering was led by สฟAbd Allฤh b. สพUbay b. Salลซl, and he's their chief and leader, . In addition, there's an even more clear proof for that: the Prophet ๏ทบ All those who took the burden of reconciling interpretations had Suhayl's แธฅadฤซth from his day โdo not initiate the greeting of peace with polytheistsโ as the only .[112]

He told him to greet that group, and that was a party of angels sitting there, and listen to the response that they give him, for it would form his greeting and that of his offspring. He then went away and said: Peace be upon you! They (the angels) said: May there be peace upon you and the Mercy of God, and they made an addition of" Mercy of God". .[113]

And this is explicitly clear on that this particular greeting is general, the greeting of Adam and his children, that his sons use to greet one another.

All that we have mentioned earlier from Qurสพฤnic proofs and famous authentic Prophetic แธฅadฤซths point to the correctness of the opinion of Abลซ สพUmฤmah al-Bฤhilฤซy, สฟAbd สฟAllฤh b. Masสฟลซd, Faแธฤlah b. สฟUbayd, Abลซ al-Dardฤสพ and Ibn สฟAbbฤs โ May God be pleased with them โ and those who agreed with them on that itโs permissible to initiate the greeting of peace with non-Muslims. And there are no companions who differ with them except on what is narrated from:

  V. ELUCIDATING THE CORRECT VIEW:

What emerges as the correct view from the collection of all these แธฅadฤซths is that there's no prohibition from initiating the greeting of peace with non-Muslims, except in only one circumstance: in the case of war , โ may God be pleased with them โ

ูุงูุตุญูุญ ูู ูุฐู ุงูุฃุญุงุฏูุซ ูููุง ุฃูู ูุง ูููุน ูู ุงุจุชุฏุงุก ุฃุญุฏ ุจุงูุณูุงู ูู ุบูุฑ ุงููุณูููู ุฅูุง ูู ุญุงู ูุงุญุฏุฉ ููู ุญุงู ุงูุญุฑุจุ ุญุชู ูุง ูููู ุฃูุงูุงุ ุชุชุฑุชุจ ุนููู ุฃุญูุงู ุงูุฃูุงูุ ุฃูุง ูุง ุนุฏุง ุฐูู ููุณุชุญุจ ุฅูุดุงุก ุงูุณูุงู ุนูู ูู ุฃุญุฏ ูุณูู ูุงู ุฃู ุบูุฑ ูุณููุ ููุง ุฌุงุก ุนู ุฃูุซุฑ ุงูุตุญุงุจุฉ ุงูุฐูู ูุฑุฏ ุนููู ููู ูู ูุฐู ุงููุณุฃูุฉ ุฑุถู ุงููู ุนููู.

al-Qurแนญubฤซ argued[131] that the apparent meaning from the Qurสพฤn indicates the permissibility of initiating the greeting of peace with them based on the generality of the texts, and he said: โThe permissibility of initiating the greeting of peace with non-Muslims was stated by some of the Pious Predecessors (Salaf). Ibn สฟUyaynah replied in the affirmative when asked whether initiating the greeting of peace with non-Muslims was permissible, and he cited the verse, โGod does not forbid you to deal kindly and justly with anyone who has not fought you for your faith or driven you out of your homes: God loves the justโ, and โYou have a good example in Abrahamโ, and he said to his [non-Muslim] dad: โPeace be with youโ. salih = righteous

In addition, one should greet back polytheists according to the correct view, which is the majority opnion. al-Qurแนญubฤซ said: โThere was some difference of opinion concerning greeting back people of the covenant (สพahl al-dhimmah) with the greeting of peace: is it obligatory just like with greeting back Muslims? That was the opinion of Ibn สฟAbbฤs, al-Shaสฟbiy and Qatฤdah, based on the generality of the verse (Q.4:86), and the order to greet them back in the authentic Sunnah.โ[135]

In all other cases, if they greet with , what is obligatory by the Book is to respond with a better one โ which is the preferable choice as evidenced by or returning it in a similar form. This entails not , just as it's apparent from the verse: โBut when you [believers] are offered a greeting, respond with a better one, or at least return it.โ[137]

ุฃูุง ูุง ุนุฏุง ุฐููุ ูุฅุฐุง ุญููุง ุจุชุญูุฉ ุทูุจุฉุ ูุงููุฃููุฑ ุจู ุจูุต ุงููุชุงุจ ุงูุฑุฏ ุจุงูุฃุญุณู ููู ุงูุฃูุถู ููุง ูููุฏู ุชูุฏูู ุฐูู ูู ุณูุงู ุงูุขูุฉ[136] ุฃู ุฑุฏูุง ููุง ููุ ูุนุฏู ุงูุงูุชุตุงุฑ ุนูู ูุง ูู ุฏูููุง ููุง ูู ุธุงูุฑ ูููู ุชุนุงูู{ูุฅุฐุง ุญููุชู ุจุชุญูุฉ ูุญููุง ุจุฃุญุณู ูููุง ุฃู ุฑุฏููุง}[137].

And this is the opinion of Ibn สฟAbbฤs, for he says: โGreet back with peace to Jews, Christians, or Zoroastrians, since God says: โBut when you [believers] are offered a greeting, respond with a better one, or at least return itโ.โ[138]

Moreover, the generality of the verse also includes the case in which a polytheist says โmay the Peace, Mercy and Blessings of God be bestowed upon youโ. As such, it is obligatory to greet him back with that same expression. In addition, it was authentically narrated that Ibn สฟAbbฤs said, โIf Pharaoh had said to me, โMay God bless you,โ I would have said, โAnd you too.โ But Pharaoh is dead."[139]

al-Bukhฤrฤซ included it in al-Adab al-Mufradุงู in the chapter โHow to supplicate for a non-Muslim under our protection.โ The intent of Ibn สฟAbbฤs was to show the permissibility of supplicating for non-Muslims with .

ููุฏ ุฃูุฑุฏู ุงูุจุฎุงุฑู ูู ุงูุฃุฏุจ ุงูููุฑุฏ ูู ุจุงุจ(ููู ูุฏุนู ููุฐูู)ุ ูููุตูุฏ ุงุจู ุนุจุงุณ ุจูุงู ูุดุฑูุนูุฉ ุงูุฏุนุงุก ูุบูุฑ ุงููุณูู ุจุงูุจุฑูุฉ ูุงูุฎูุฑุ ููุง ูุฑุฏ ุนู ุงุจู ุนูุฑ ูุนูุจุฉ ุจู ุนุงูุฑ ูู ุฃูููุง ุฏุนูุง ูุฐูู(ุฃูุซุฑ ุงููู ูุงูู ูููุฏู)ุ ููู ุงูุจุฑูุฉ ุงูุฏููููุฉ!

Ibn Qayyim stated, โHow do we greet them back if itโs established that they said to us โPeace be upon youโ? If itโs sure that the [Answer:] What the evidence from the Sharฤซสฟah and its principles dictate is that he shall be responded with โAnd peace be upon youโ. For this classifies as justice, and God ordains justice and kindness, and He said: โBut when you [believers] are offered a greeting, respond with a better one, or at least return it.โ. โ[140]

Supplication for non-Muslims with goodness, prosperity, and blessings is permissible, as indicated by the verse concerning parents โ even if theyโre polytheists, โAnd lower your wing in humility towards them in kindness and say, โLord, have mercy on them, just as they cared for me when I was littleโ.โ[141]

al-แนฌabarฤซ said: โAnd a group of scholars interpreted the verse: โIt is not fitting for the Prophet and the believers to ask forgiveness for the idolaters โ even if they are related to them ...โ[142] that God prohibited asking forgiveness for idolaters after their death, as the verse continues: โafter having been shown that they are the inhabitants of the Blazeโ. And they added: No one is sure about that [from an idolater] except if he dies while heโs an unbeliever. This is in contrast to when heโs still alive, and there is no way to know for sure , so believers may ask forgiveness for them.โ

shahid = witness

As such, it has been established that this แธฅadฤซth came in the context of a story that elucidates its meaning, and that it isn't general, nor absolute. Furthermore, Suhayl shortned it causing thereby a disruption, or he forgot, or he and his dade made independent reasoning by making analogy between the People of the Book and Christians that he used to meet in Syria, and between the Jews that were mentioned in the แธฅadฤซth. Or he may have taken it to be general.

ูุซุจุช ุฃู ู ูุฐุง ุงูุญุฏูุซ ุฌุงุก ูู ุณูุงู ูุตุฉ ุชูุดู ุนู ูุนูุงูุ ูุฃูู ููุณ ุนูู ุนููููุ ููุง ุนูู ุฅุทูุงููุ ูุฃู ุณููู ุงุฎุชุตุฑู ูุฃุฎู ูููุ ุฃู ูุณููุ ุฃู ุฃูู ูู ุฃู ุฃุจูู ุงุฌุชูุฏ ูู ููุงุณ ุฃูู ุงููุชุงุจ ูุงููุตุงุฑู ุงูุฐูู ูุงู ูุฌุฏูู ูู ุงูุดุงู ุนูู ุงููููุฏ ุงูุฐูู ูุฑุฏ ูููู ุงูุญุฏูุซุ ุฃู ุญูู ุงูุญุฏูุซ ุนูู ุนูููู ุงุฌุชูุงุฏุง ูููุ ุจูููุง ุฑูุงู ุฃุจู ุจุตุฑุฉ ุงูุบูุงุฑู ูุฃุจู ุนุจุฏ ุงูุฑุญูู ุงูุฌููู ูุนุจุฏ ุงููู ุจู ุนูุฑุ ูู ุณูุงู ุฎุฑูุฌ ุงููุจู ุตูู ุงููู ุนููู ูุณูู ูุญุตุงุฑ ุจูู ูุฑูุถุฉุ ูููู ุฃุตุญุงุจู ุนู ุงุจุชุฏุงุฆูู ุจุงูุณูุงูุ ูุฃูุฑูู ุฃู ููุชุตุฑูุง ุจุงูุฑุฏ ุนูู(ูุนูููู)ุ ุญุชู ูุง ูููู ุฃูุงูุง ูููุน ูู ุญุฑุจููุ ููุง ุฃูุฑูู ุจุงูุชุถููู ุนูููู ูู ุงูุทุฑูู ููุณุจุจ ุฐุงุชู ููู ุฃูู ุฌุงุก ูุญุฑุจูู.

Fourthly: In addition, there came many general authentic แธฅadฤซths from a number of companions โ among them al-Barฤสพ b. สฟฤzib, สฟAbd Allฤh b. Salฤm, สฟAbd Allฤh b. สฟAmrลซ, and Abลซ สพUmฤmah al-Bฤhilฤซy โ that command spreading the greeting of peace to the whole world, with those you know and those you do not know, and it is in accordance with the apparent meaning of Qurสพฤnic verses.

Fifthly: The practical Sunnah of the Prophet ๏ทบ is in accordance with his sayings: It was authenticatly narrated that he came to a gathering in which there were Muslims, pagan idolators and Jews, and he greeted them all with peace, then he invited them to God and also recited to them verses from the Qurสพฤn.

Sixthly: It was established from a number of companions such as Ibn Masสฟลซd, Abลซ สพUmฤmah al-Bฤhilฤซy, and narrated from Faแธฤlah b. สฟUbayd, Abลซ al-Dardฤสพ and Ibn สฟAbbฤs that they were initiating the greeting of peace with non-Muslims, or they greeted everyone they encountered be it a Muslim or non-Muslim, basing this on the generality of the Qurสพฤnic and Prophetic texts. And among those who held the permissibility of this are al-Nakhaสฟฤซ, Ibn สฟUyaynah and al-สพAwzฤสฟฤซ. Moreover, al-Qurแนญubฤซ maintained that this was indeed the apparent meaning from the Qurสพฤnic texts, if not for the แธฅadฤซth of Suhayl. Ishฬฃฤq b. Rฤhawayh and al-แนฌabarฤซ agreed with them if there was a reason that required initiating the greeting of peace, such as in a companionship, or neighborhood, or travel, or in the case of a need, or other similar reasons. The correct view however is its absolute permissibility because of the generality of the evidence. The prohibition of initiating the greeting of peace with them concerns only the case of war.

Seventhly: What is established concerning greeting back anyone โ whether Muslim or non-Muslim โ is to greet with something better, or similar, just as the generality of this verse suggests, โBut when you [believers] are offered a greeting, respond with a better one, or at least return it.โ

Heightly: Greeting back with the mere expression โand to youโ is restricted to only two circumstances: The first one concerns the case of war, with the implicit reason that the utterance of peace The second one, in the case of harm and supplicating with evil in the greeting, , and this and its guidance and kindness to the creation.

ุซุงููุง:ูุฅู ุงูุงูุชุตุงุฑ ูู ุงูุฑุฏ ุนูู ุบูุฑ ุงููุณูููู ุจููู(ูุนูููู)ุฅููุง ูู ูู ุญุงููู ุงูุฃููู ุญุงู ุงูุญุฑุจ ุญุชู ูุง ูููู ุฐูุฑ ุงูุณูุงู ุฃูุงูุงุ ูุงูุซุงููุฉ ูู ุญุงู ุงูุฅุณุงุกุฉ ูุงูุฏุนุงุก ุจุงูุดุฑ ูู ุงูุชุญูุฉุ ูููุชุตุฑ ูู ุงูุฑุฏ ุนูู (ูุนูููู)ุ ููุง ูุฒุงุฏ ุนูู ุฐููุ ููุฐุง ูู ุฃุฏุจ ุงูุฅุณูุงู ููุฏูู ูุฑููู ุจุงูุฎูู.

Ninthly: Also if a non-Muslim greets a Muslim with the expression โmay the Peace, Mercy and Blessings of God be bestowed upon youโ then itโs necessary to return oneโs greeting with that same expression, as argued by Ibn Qayyim, based on the Qurสพฤnic texts to this effect.

Tenthly: These Qurสพฤnic and Prophetic Manners are among the virtues of Islฤm and its mercy to mankind, and kindness that extends to all creation, and among the perfection of the Sharฤซสฟah that came with justice, equity, kindness, and mercy in organizing the relation between Muslims and others.

  TRANSLATORโS NOTE:

^ : I use the expression โthe greeting of peaceโ (al-Salฤm) to exclusively refer to the Islamic greeting al-Salฤmu สฟAlaykum (Peace be upon you). It is worthy of note here that all scholars agree that initiating regular greetings with non-Muslims such as โHelloโ, โGood dayโ, and other similar greetings is permissible; the difference of opinion concerns only the aforementioned expression (some of those who argue for it being non permissible mention that this specific phrase is specific to the Muslim Ummah only as a justification).
